# Devops Foundations

> DevOps ensures collaboration and communication between software engineers (Dev) and IT operations (Ops). With DevOps, changes make it to production faster. Resources are easier to share. And large-scale systems are easier to manage and maintain. In this course, well-known DevOps practitioners Ernest Mueller and James Wickett provide an overview of the DevOps movement, focusing on the core value of

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205)
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

#### [The foundations of DevOps](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=0)** - [[DevOps]] is a collaborative way of delivering software and systems that improves your technical and business outcomes, and working environments.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=8)** - But the universe of modern technology is vast, and there are many people in it that speak different languages and have different skills.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=14)** - They don't always get along, but in the end they all have to work together to create solutions, and that's what DevOps does.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=20)** Howdy, I'm Ernest.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=22)** - And I'm James.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=23)** We've applied the principles and practices of DevOps in many different types of organizations, and we've seen it pay off.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=28)** You'll learn new skills and abilities to apply DevOps to the people, processes, and technology in your team and organization.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=35)** - We'll also level up your understanding of key areas like [[Continuous Delivery (CD)|continuous delivery]], [[Infrastructure as code (IaC)|infrastructure as code]] and site reliability engineering.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=43)** - When you're done learning these DevOps concepts, you'll have the tools to embark on your own DevOps journey of discovery.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/the-foundations-of-devops?u=76281980&t=48)** - Let's get underway.

### 1. DevOps Basics

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### [What is DevOps?](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=1)** - [[DevOps]], you've probably seen the term or heard it used, but it's not always clear what people mean by it.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=6)** Okay, so let me ask you, Ernest, what do you think it means?
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=10)** - The term DevOps itself combines two traditional roles in tech, the developers, who typically write application code, and the operations engineers, who set up and manage the systems that the applications run on top of.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=23)** These two bodies of work combine to create an overall service that people can use.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=28)** - But these roles keep changing as technology changes.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=31)** And in the late 2000s, it became clear that it didn't make sense to keep these roles as two completely disconnected groups.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=37)** And so DevOps was born.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=40)** - [Ernest] DevOps is the practice of operations and development engineers working together through the entire service lifecycle, from the design and development process, all the way to production support, including both the applications and the systems.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=56)** - Of course, there are lots of specialized roles in the IT world.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=59)** Front end devs, test engineers, build engineers, networking engineers, and security engineers, to name a few.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=66)** The intent is to bring them all together to collaborate instead of just having them do their work in isolation and hoping that everything works smoothly when finally brought together.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=75)** - Even the database admins?
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=77)** - Ah yes, even the DBAs fit inside of DevOps, everyone who practices and participates in creating and running a service.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=85)** - DevOps is also characterized by operations engineers using development techniques for their systems work
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=92)** - In DevOps, systems engineering works just like a [[Software Development]] workflow.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=97)** Code to create, configure, and operate the system is checked into source control to go through build, test, and deployment.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=105)** It's a change from the largely manual [[System Administration]] processes of the past.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=110)** - But we understand that that's a broad enough definition.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=113)** It doesn't really tell you much about what it is.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=116)** We like to break explaining DevOps down into three levels, the values, the principles, and the practices.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=123)** - We'll discuss these three levels in the course.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=126)** But first, let's address the big question.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=130)** Why should you care? What can DevOps do for you?
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=133)** And why would you want to practice it?
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=135)** - The bottom line is that DevOps is shown to be effective in improving both IT and business outcomes.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=142)** [[Google]]'s DevOps Research and Assessment Team does an annual global survey of all kinds of IT organizations to perform statistically sound analysis on what IT practices correlate to successful business results.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=156)** The 2021 State of DevOps Report indicated that there's a big difference between elite and low-performing IT teams, and that the gap is getting larger.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=166)** Elite teams deployed changes 973 times more frequently with 6,570 times shorter lead times than low IT performers.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=177)** And while you might think that moving more quickly would produce lower quality, instead, they had three times fewer failures and recovered from issues 6,570 times faster than those low-performing organizations.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=191)** And those elite teams are much more likely to be using DevOps practices like [[Continuous Integration (CI)|continuous integration]], site reliability engineering, and deployment automation.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=201)** - Statistically, companies that are high IT performers spend 22% less time on unplanned work and rework, and they're more than twice as likely to achieve their organizational objectives, ship [[Microsoft Products|products]], and attain customer satisfaction.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=216)** And perhaps most importantly for those of us who do the work, this heightened productivity actually makes practitioners half as likely to suffer from burnout.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=226)** These benefits are huge.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=227)** - Absolutely, James, and the survey showed that these results held true across different sizes and types of businesses, including for-profit and not-for-profit organizations.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=238)** - It also works for both product engineering type organizations and internal IT organizations.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=243)** Different DevOps practices and tools are more relevant for one type of work or another, but at a high level, the principles and methods help all kinds of technology teams.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=253)** So, Ernest and I, we've been practicing DevOps since it started and it's helped us both deliver solutions in a variety of companies for more than a decade now.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=262)** - And this section wouldn't be complete without saying what DevOps is not.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=267)** It's not just a new name for an operations team, or a new name for an existing job title.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=273)** It's not one person doing every single job, and it doesn't require using any specific tool.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=279)** - Keep in mind that a lot of people use the term DevOps without really understanding what it means.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=285)** So always check what you're hearing against the core concepts of DevOps.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=289)** - And maybe invite those people to take this course.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/what-is-devops?u=76281980&t=292)** - Yep, DevOps has plenty of room for everyone.

#### [DevOps core values: CAMS](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=0)** - The CAMS model, created by [[DevOps]] pioneers [[John the Ripper|John]] Willis and Damon Edwards, stands for Culture, Automation, Measurement, and Sharing.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=10)** CAMS has become the model set of values used by many DevOps practitioners.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=15)** Patrick Debois, he's often referred to as the godfather of DevOps since he did coin the term, says, "DevOps is a human problem."
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=23)** Well, DevOps is often thought of as a technology problem.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=26)** At its heart, it's a people and cultural problem, but what is culture?
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=32)** Culture is, you know, a lot more than ping pong tables in the [[Microsoft Office|office]] or free food in the company cafeteria.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=38)** Culture is driven by human behavior.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=41)** Culture exists among people with a mutual understanding of each other and where they're coming from.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=47)** Early on, IT organizations split their teams into two major groups.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=52)** The first group, development, was charged with creating applications and features, usually as fast and as cutting edge as possible.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=60)** The other group, operations, was charged with server and network maintenance, stability, security, controlling costs, and generally making sure everything turned out right.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=70)** As time passed, as you might have guessed, virtual walls were formed around these groups, making silos, due to their differing goals.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=78)** After that pattern had decades to become rigid, these groups didn't speak the same language or have a mutual understanding anymore, and that leads to conflict and only caring about your team's goals and not the overall business outcome.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=92)** Changing these underlying behaviors and assumptions is how you drive change in your company's culture, and it's where you'll want to start.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=100)** This brings us to A in CAMS, Automation.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=104)** The first thing people think about when they think of DevOps is usually automation.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=108)** Now, DevOps is not just about automated tooling.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=111)** Jumping into automation without spending time on the [[Representational State Transfer (REST)|rest]] of the values is one of the main ways that people fail at DevOps implementation.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=119)** That said, automation is a critical part of your DevOps journey.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=123)** Once you begin to understand your culture, you can create a fabric of automation that allows you to create and control your systems and applications.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=131)** Automation is the accelerator that helps you unlock the other benefits of DevOps.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=136)** Manual work is the source of many inefficiencies and quality problems in technology value streams, so you want to make automation your primary approach to creating solutions.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=146)** Okay, next up is the M in CAMS, which stands for Measurement.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=150)** One of the keys to a rational approach to technology is your ability to observe and measure what's going on, both in your systems and with your people.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=158)** Metrics tell you what is happening and whether the changes you've made have improved things.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=163)** Now, there's two major pitfalls with metrics.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=166)** First, sometimes we choose to watch the wrong things.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=169)** Second, sometimes we incentivize them improperly.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=174)** Because of this, DevOps strongly advises you to measure key metrics that measure outcomes across organizations, things like mean time to restore service after an outage and cycle time to deploy a new feature, but also consider higher level results like costs, revenue, and even employee satisfaction.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=193)** These are all a part of generating holistic insight into your system.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=197)** They help engage the team towards your overall goal.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=200)** Then you can share them internally or even externally with customers and partners.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=205)** Okay, speaking of sharing, that's the S in CAMS.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=209)** Sharing ideas and problems is the heart of collaboration, and it's also at the heart of DevOps.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=215)** Teamwork, transparency, and collaboration are key attributes to allow your team to learn and improve the larger organization.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=222)** Sharing information via documentation, pair programming, peer reviews, mentoring, inclusion, and so on, it just makes everyone stronger and improves your technical and business outcomes.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=234)** Adopting CAMS as the core values of DevOps reminds us that fundamentally, we are looking to change people's behavior, we can use the automation to accelerate change, we need to measure what we're doing to improve it, and working together builds better services.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=251)** That's the core approach behind many of the more specific techniques we'll cover later in the course.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-core-values-cams?u=76281980&t=257)** Take these values to heart because the rest of your DevOps journey is about trying to realize them in your organization.

#### [DevOps guiding principles: The Three Ways](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=0)** - Let's talk about strategic principles you can use to take the core [[DevOps]] values and bring them to life.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=7)** The most respected set of principles is called the Three Ways of DevOps.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=12)** They were developed by Gene Kim, author of the "Phoenix Project" and "The DevOps Handbook", and Mike Orzen, author of "Lean IT."
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=20)** The three ways are systems thinking and the principles of flow, amplifying feedback loops, and a culture of continuous experimentation and learning.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=31)** The first way systems thinking and the principles of flow tells us that we should make sure and focus on the overall outcome of the entire system.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=40)** It's easy to make the mistake of optimizing one part of the value chain at the expense of overall results.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=47)** For example, when you're trying to optimize performance in an application, increasing performance or system resources in one area causes the bottleneck to move sometimes to unexpected places.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=58)** Adding more application servers for a good example can overwhelm a database server with connections and bring it down.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=66)** You have to understand the whole system to optimize it well.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=69)** This same principle applies to IT organizations.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=73)** A deployment team might establish processes to make their own work go smoothly and their productivity numbers look good, but those same changes can compromise the development process and reduce the organization's overall ability to deliver solutions.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=89)** If you ride all the software in the world, but you can't deliver it to a customer in a way that they can use it, you lose.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=96)** Handoffs and friction between parts of the organization that participate in delivering something is often where the flow from concept to cash goes wrong.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=106)** Use systems thinking as guidance when defining success metrics and evaluating the outcome of changes.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=113)** And remember that overall flow from beginning to end is how you actually produce value.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=121)** The second way, amplifying feedback loops is all about creating, shortening, and amplifying feedback loops between the parts of the organization that are in the flow of the value chain.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=133)** A feedback loop is just a process that takes its own output into consideration when deciding what to do next.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=139)** The term originally comes from engineering control systems.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=143)** Short, effective feedback loops are the key to productive [[Product Development]], [[Software Development]] and operations.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=151)** Take the story of a simple code bug.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=154)** If that bug is found by the developer before they check it into source control because unit tests on their desktop caught it, you've eliminated a problem with very little time wasted.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=165)** But if that bug slips by and is found by a QA team and is documented in a ticketing system and then pushed back to a developer to fix, it's still resolved, but with more time wasted.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=178)** If it gets all the way into a customer release and is encountered by end users logged with a support organization, churn over in support, escalated back to development reprioritized by a product manager and then fixed, it wastes even more time and money for a same or worse outcome.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=199)** Effective and fast feedback yields a better and more efficient system.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=203)** Use amplifying feedback loops to help you when you're creating multi-team processes, visualizing metrics and designing delivery flows.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=212)** The third way.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=213)** A culture of continuous experimentation and learning reminds us to create a work culture that allows for both continuous experimentation and learning.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=223)** You and your team should be open to learning new things, and the best route to that is actively trying them out to see what works and what doesn't work, and adjusting and iterating.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=233)** Instead of falling into analysis paralysis.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=236)** It also means engaging in the continuous practice required to master the skills and tools that are already part of your portfolio.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=244)** You master your skills by the repetition of practice and you find new skills by picking them up and actually trying them.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=252)** You may have heard technologists say things like working code wins.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=256)** If it hurts, do it more often and fail fast.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=260)** These all speak to this kind of culture which learns by retaining a practical focus on doing instead of just talking about doing.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=268)** Use a culture of continuous experimentation and learning when creating team processes and standards and as part of your leadership style, encourage sharing and trying new ideas.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=281)** The three ways provide a practical framework to take the core DevOps values of cams and effectively implement specific processes and tools in alignment with them.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=291)** As you move forward in your DevOps implementation.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/devops-guiding-principles-the-three-ways?u=76281980&t=293)** Always keep thinking about the whole system, asking yourself how you can build in more feedback loops and seeing how you can create an environment that facilitates experimentation and learning.

#### [Your DevOps practice playbook](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/your-devops-practice-playbook?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/your-devops-practice-playbook?u=76281980&t=1)** - In [[Agile Development|agile]], there are structured methodologies like [[Scrum]] and extreme programming that provide a highly prescriptive playbook for implementing Agile in an organization.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/your-devops-practice-playbook?u=76281980&t=10)** In [[DevOps]], we don't have a strictly defined approach of that sort, but some common patterns have emerged to guide a DevOps implementation.
>

> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/your-devops-practice-playbook?u=76281980&t=36)** This is the people part of DevOps that you've already seen reflected in our core values.

#### [Which DevOps tools should I use?](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=0)** - You may be wondering how we've gotten this far into our course on [[DevOps]] without talking about tools.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=6)** - [[Kubernetes]], [[Terraform]], [[Ansible]], Puppet, Chef, [[GitHub]].

>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=18)** There's a reason we've held off talking about tools until now.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=21)** One of the earliest pieces of DevOps Wisdom was coined by Alex Honor, an early DevOps consultant and creator of the Runbook Automation tool, Rundeck.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=30)** The phrase is this, "People over process over tools."
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=35)** In short, it recommends identifying who is responsible for a job function first, and making sure that they have the skills and support they need.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=44)** Then, defining the process that needs to happen around them and their work, and then only after all that, selecting and implementing the tools to perform that process, choosing the one that best fits your own needs.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=58)** - It seems somewhat obvious, but technical workers and sometimes overzealous managers under the sway of a tech vendor salesperson are awfully tempted to do the reverse, focusing on tools first, then processes, and then maybe, if they get to it, the people.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=76)** But there is no such thing as the best tool.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=79)** There's only the best tool for you and your specific situation.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=83)** - That's right, and people doesn't mean just you.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=87)** Remember that DevOps is sharing.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=89)** How does the tool make everyone collaborate better?
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=92)** - That's right, the best tools are ones that all the participants in the value stream can use effectively.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=98)** - We do want to give you some advice on how to choose tools, though.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=102)** The first and best guidance we can give is the KISS principle, which is pretty well known both in the US military and in [[Software Development]].
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=110)** - Keep it super secret?
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=112)** - No, it stands for keep it simple, stupid.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=115)** - Good call.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=117)** While tools are great and help you do things, in tech, it's really easy to get too many tools.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=123)** Every single tool you use has to be learned, implemented, upgraded, secured, and integrated with other tools.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=130)** Yeah, complexity has become a major problem in tech.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=133)** Here's an example of just a part of the cloud native computing foundation's landscape diagram.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=139)** Basically, all the pieces you can add in or swap out of Kubernetes.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=144)** - I'll be honest, after DevOps began, I saw a lot of companies getting much better as they put together good, coherent, [[Continuous Delivery (CD)|continuous delivery]], observability, and [[Infrastructure as code (IaC)|infrastructure as code]] implementations.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=156)** In recent years, though, I've been seeing the average quality of those implementations go down, and increased complexity is one of the major causes.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=165)** It's really easy to download and install a giant suite of technical tools nowadays, but every time you do, you put a giant weight around your neck that'll hold you back from moving quickly in the future.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=177)** - Yeah, you know, Ernest, I've been seeing the same thing in [[Cybersecurity]], too many tools poorly thought out and tough to implement, causing worse outcomes.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=187)** - The second thing you need to keep in mind is that you need all of your tools to integrate well and operate in a dynamic environment.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=195)** - In DevOps, we frequently refer to our tools as a tool chain.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=199)** Good tools don't live in isolation.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=201)** You need your build tool, deploy tool, observability tool, and so on to integrate so you can [[Jetpack Compose|compose]] a solution out of them easily.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=209)** - A good example of this composability is the Linux command line, where all commands can have their output piped into the input of another command, allowing you to chain tools together.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=220)** - And in the dynamic world of modern virtual servers, applications, and containers, you need those tools to be able to automatically adapt.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=228)** - I still remember being really agitated at a security vendor that insisted I enter all my cloud servers' IP addresses into their product's dashboard.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=238)** I told them, "This isn't the 1970s, the number of cloud servers and their network addresses is going to change every five minutes forever.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=246)** Get me a product that has an API."
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=248)** - As we talk through the five pillars, we'll mention specific tools that can help, but remember, pick the tools that work for your organization and processes and promote collaboration and sharing among your people.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=261)** Don't add on more tools than you need, keep it simple, and put a high priority on tools being able to integrate with others and dynamically adapt to a changing environment.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/which-devops-tools-should-i-use?u=76281980&t=271)** - If you have your own suggestions on how to best select tools, please share them as a comment in the course Q&A section.

>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/why-do-we-need-a-devops-culture?u=76281980&t=89)** This creates a division between groups that should share a common goal.

>

> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/why-do-we-need-a-devops-culture?u=76281980&t=118)** We'd work with that team to negotiate specifications, then it would go through the procurement process, be ordered from the supplier, delivered, racked and installed in the data center, get the operating system loaded, and finally handed over to us.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/why-do-we-need-a-devops-culture?u=76281980&t=133)** Then, we'd put on application servers and the like and give it to the developers usually way after they needed them.

>

>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/why-do-we-need-a-devops-culture?u=76281980&t=238)** But, these approaches cause as many new issues as they solve.

>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/why-do-we-need-a-devops-culture?u=76281980&t=250)** How can we change our culture when this model and our behaviors based on its assumptions have become so ingrained?

>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/why-do-we-need-a-devops-culture?u=76281980&t=271)** - But change is hard, and is easier said than done.
>

>

#### [Communication and trust power DevOps](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=0)** - Communication and trust are a key part of a productive [[DevOps]] culture.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=5)** - I've seen projects from application deployments to network upgrades to corporate acquisitions succeed or fail based on the quality of communication.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=15)** Without building a culture of communication and trust, you'll find that attempts to implement specific technical practices will go wrong, sabotaged either deliberately because of competing goals, or inadvertently because of lack of understanding.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=31)** - Most people would agree that communication's important, but how do we do it well?
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=37)** - Good communication requires more than just reminding people to write documentation or post in chat.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=43)** - [James] Right, you want to be mindful of how to set up communication channels.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=47)** If you intend information to flow to others, there should be a place and time you all agree on to communicate.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=53)** - [Instructor] Have published standards.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=55)** Here's the file repository all customer information will go into.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=59)** Here's the chat channel all downtime incident communication will go into.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=64)** Here's the email alias that software release communication will go to.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=68)** - You know, good communication doesn't just happen.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=70)** It requires a plan, especially for fast moving organizations or high-pressure situations like outages.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=77)** You should have processes that say when and to whom people need to communicate around business events.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=82)** In fact, please take a minute and share what communication techniques work best for your organization in the course Q&A so we can keep this conversation on best practices going.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=94)** - [Instructor] Communication and transparency gets people information that they need, but even more importantly, it builds trust.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=102)** - Sociologist Ron Westrum created a model based on his research showing three major types of organizations and the resulting information flow.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=111)** Organizations that work simply by everyone looking out for their own needs, which he calls pathological organizations, organizations that focus on strictly defined roles and teams defending their turf, those are bureaucratic organizations, and organizations that focus on the mission result in a generative style, which have the most effective information flow.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=134)** - Research across many fields, healthcare, aviation, tech, shows that good information flow results in better organizational safety, organizational performance, and productivity.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=147)** Creating a generative organization requires building an environment of high trust, where otherwise bad news is welcomed.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=155)** Those who bring it are trained and celebrated, and it's used to learn and improve.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=161)** - But how do you build trust and respect and eliminate blame and hostility so that people feel safe to work together and to take chances to innovate?
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=171)** - Well, first, not everyone has good social skills and can have challenges with successfully interacting with people.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=178)** I personally went from painfully introverted as a young man to an abrasive engineer in my early career before I realized how important communication skills are to success, and I put work into building them.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=191)** - Well, now you're smooth as silk.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=194)** I've had a different journey, being a little bit more extroverted by nature, but I've also had to work on communication a lot throughout my career.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=201)** - There's a set of books that we've both found helpful, like "How to Win Friends and Influence People," "Crucial Conversations," "How to Say It At Work," and others that we've put in the course handout.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=213)** If you find it challenging to have friendly, successful interactions with other people, or if you have difficult relationships to navigate, you could make a goal to read one of these books per quarter to improve.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=225)** - Beyond that, the single biggest impediment to trust in an organization is misunderstanding due to lack of context.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=233)** It's very rare that someone is acting out of malice.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=236)** Most people are honestly trying to do a good job in the way that they think is best, given the constraints that they perceive.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=242)** Assume good faith when information is lacking.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=246)** - Someone else's job is always easier, isn't it?
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=249)** When James and I were first working together, I had a senior developer confront me as the leader of our web operations team, frustrated that his project wasn't higher on our priority list.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=260)** He said, "I don't know why we need your team anyway.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=263)** All you guys do is move files around."
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=266)** Of course, I had an overworked team of operations engineers doing software deployments, building new servers, improving our monitoring, handling a large load of on-call incidents, performing all of our [[Cybersecurity]], and more.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=281)** While that developer could probably have benefited from a lesson in respectful language, a large part of their frustration came from just plain not knowing what our team was doing.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=291)** - The fix wasn't to recoil from that or fight back, but lean into communication.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=296)** We set up a program including the development teams, operations teams, and business teams to create shared goals and provide visibility into how we all were working together.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=305)** This promoted understanding and things worked a lot better after that.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=310)** - You know, the IT security world has done a pretty good job of teaching everyone about least privilege and separation of duties.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=318)** Unfortunately, these terms often become a knee jerk justification for locking access down way past what any real world compliance requires.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=328)** - Transparency and teamwork have business value.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=331)** Don't settle for restricting communication without a compelling reason when there's value in sharing.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=336)** You know, there's no shortcut to building mutual trust.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=339)** It develops over time.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=341)** - People fear what they don't understand.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=344)** Be open, be transparent.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=346)** Let people get context even if you're not there personally to give it to them.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=351)** That means let them come into your chat rooms, see your team Wiki pages, see your code, your infrastructure, your monitoring tool, your ticket tracker.
>
> **[6:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=360)** Always think about what you could communicate that will help others do their job or understand your context better.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=368)** Remember, sharing is a key part of our values in CAMS and the feedback loops of the three ways depend on information flow.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=376)** - And on the flip side, be curious and respectful.
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=379)** You're working with good people.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=381)** Try to understand their perspective so you can align your goals with them.
>
> **[6:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/communication-and-trust-power-devops?u=76281980&t=386)** Focus on shared goals, and show that you value others and their needs.

#### [Collaboration: Break silos in case of DevOps](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=1)** - Collaboration towards a common goal is the secret sauce to making [[DevOps]] work.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=5)** Yet, we've already talked about the wall of confusion that creates a division between groups that should share a common goal.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=12)** - It's often assumed that these divisions are caused by the stereotype that technology professionals just have poor people skills.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=20)** While communication is an important part of solving the problem, this overlooks the institutional causes of the wall of confusion.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=28)** - That's right.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=29)** The real cause is that the institution is incentivizing opposing behavior.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=34)** - In the classic shop, the development teams are charged with developing new functionality, making changes, and moving as fast as possible.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=43)** - At the same time, operations teams are charged with the conflicting responsibilities of maintaining stability and controlling change.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=51)** Then those teams are given goals and metrics that only care about their individual role, and encourage them to pursue that goal, speed or stability, in this case, at all costs.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=62)** - This causes a harmful conflict of interest, and diminishes feedback loops.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=67)** Incentivizing groups to only care about their own areas' results creates a less optimal outcome for the organization.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=75)** This is local optimization getting in the way of global optimization.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=80)** - [Instructor] There's a concept called Conway's Law that states that when you try to [[Design Systems]], your systems will merely always align themselves to your communication boundaries.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=90)** Organizational boundaries are one type of communication boundary.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=94)** - The first wave of DevOps tells us to align around the value stream of whatever we're producing.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=100)** If your organization structure is counter to that, you're in a tight spot.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=104)** - You know, change is hard, and organizations want to uptake DevOps without having to do any hard work.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=111)** - [Ernest] Just renaming an existing team, DevOps, or making a new team called DevOps does nothing to change your communication structure or improve collaboration.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=121)** If that's all you do, don't be surprised when nothing improves.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=124)** You need real change.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=126)** - Yeah, one of the most effective techniques here is to break down team barriers, and get people from different specialties to work alongside each other in what we call cross-functional teams.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=137)** - I was working at a large [[SaaS]] company in Austin, Texas that had completely separate dev and ops teams, and life on the ops team was a never ending nightmare of developer demands interspersed with outages.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=151)** So, we started by embedding an ops engineer into a dev team that was working to roll out a new product.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=157)** He joined the team full-time, sat with them, and all of the operations tasks went into the same ticket backlog with the developer tasks, and there were some initial shock when the developer saw the huge number of epics and stories they brought with them, but then they dug in, and they realized that those were all critical items required for their new service to go live.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=178)** They had no idea all the work that went into operational readiness for a production SaaS service.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=185)** The entire team pitched in and started pulling what were previously considered ops tasks to unblock their release, and from that day on, the ops engineer was one of them, and they have nothing but respect for them, and they increasingly shared work and responsibility for the production service going forward.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=202)** - [Instructor] Well, that was a great story.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=203)** Right on, there, Ernest.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=204)** You know, by putting the right people on a team, and focusing them on a single business goal, you can maintain a very high pace, because the team isn't blocked by other teams from making progress, and isn't tempted to advocate responsibility for the end result, because it's in someone else's hands.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=223)** - But you can't just always put everybody on the same team.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=226)** Optimal team size is pretty small, given psychology research.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=230)** So, what else can you do?
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=233)** - Another great option is to set up self-service tooling to allow teams access to shared services in an automated way.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=240)** If, for example, you can get the cloud server instances you need through a self-service portal, instead of having to go log a ticket, and wait in a queue for some other person who understands nothing about your needs and use case to do it manually, well, you can drive a lot of efficiency.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=257)** - When you can't avoid having multiple teams involved in a single value flow, you need to double down on making sure they have aligned communication paths and goals.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=267)** And many times, people's roles have to change.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=270)** Developers may have to take responsibility for a failing builder deployment after they've checked in their code.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=276)** They have to be willing to go on call to support their applications in production.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=281)** Operations and QA engineers have to change their approach to provide self-service platforms and guidance instead of just doing work for other people.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=291)** - This is the three-step path to enhancing collaboration in our culture.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=295)** Reduce separate teams in the value chain by eliminating silos and creating cross-disciplinary teams, use self-service to virtually remove other teams, and align goals, and promote collaboration and mutual support in the remaining teams.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/collaboration-break-silos-in-case-of-devops?u=76281980&t=311)** - Take a minute to put some ideas in the course notebook.

#### [Continuous learning the DevOps way](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=0)** - The third way of [[DevOps]] talks about creating a culture of continuous experimentation and learning, which means mastering your own core skills as well as experimenting and taking risks in order to learn more practically.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=14)** - And you heard that a generative culture in the Western model encourages innovation and learning from failure, so how exactly do we do that?
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=23)** - In DevOps, we love Japanese words, not just because they're really cyberpunk, but also because Lean was adopted so strongly in Japan, and we get a lot of loan words back from them, like kaizen.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=35)** - Kaizen literally means change for the better, and we might roughly translate it as continuous improvement.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=41)** Kaizen is a large part of the famous Lean model of the Toyota production system, or TPS.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=48)** - Yeah, we're putting new cover sheets on all the TPS reports before they go out now.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=52)** - Yeah, not that kind of TPS.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=55)** Kaizen says the small changes people make to improve things over time can generate large results.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=61)** - Masaaki Imai's book, "Kaizen: The Key to Japan's Competitive Success," introduced kaizen to the Western world in 1986, and it's been used by companies from Lockheed Martin to Pixar Animation Studios to improve the way they operate.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=77)** It's a process that encourages everyone to look for ways to improve all parts of the job as an ongoing part of everyday work and then make small iterative changes for the better.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=89)** - There are five principles that guide kaizen.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=91)** They will sound familiar as they echo many of the points of Kim's in "The Three Ways."
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=95)** They are knowing the customer, enabling smooth workflow, going to the real place, or gemba, empowering people, and maintaining transparency.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=105)** Now, you don't have to follow a strict kaizen process, but these are all things worth thinking about in an example of how to apply DevOps culture in an organized way.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=115)** - There's a [[Microsoft Word|word]] that James mentioned that might be unfamiliar, gemba, that's worth discussing a little more.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=121)** In Japanese, it means the real place.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=124)** Kaizen emphasizes going to look at the actual place where the value's created or where the problem is, not reports, metrics, processes, or documentation about it.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=135)** It's actually going to look at it.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=138)** - That's right.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=138)** Show up in the project meeting. Go look at the code.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=141)** Go try and use the system having problems.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=144)** You know, don't rely on secondhand information or assumptions.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=147)** You know, go see.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=149)** Dr. Richard Cook, a noted physician and research scientist at Ohio State University has what he calls Cook's Rule Number 6: if they call you about a patient, go see the patient.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=161)** This is gemba.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=163)** - The kaizen improvement process, or kata, is simple, and it's a cycle of plan, do, check, act.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=173)** First, you define what you intend to do and what you expect the results to be.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=178)** Then you execute on that.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=180)** Then you measure and analyze the result and make any alterations needed, but you're doing this in small ways every day.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=187)** This isn't primarily for year-long [[Digital Transformation]] efforts.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=191)** It's a regular practice.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=193)** - If the results of your newest plan are better than the previous baseline, now it's the new baseline, and in any event, it might suggest subsequent plan, do, check, act cycles.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=205)** - This cycle shouldn't sound too new to you.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=207)** It's basically a more tactical form of the scientific method we all got taught in school.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=211)** - Oh, yeah. Yeah, I remember that.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=214)** - Yeah, but it's surprising how often we don't apply it to our business activities, instead, using one of the popular variations like plan, don't do, hide, try to make it to Friday.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=225)** - Well, they say everybody is working for the weekend.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=229)** - Everybody needs a second chance.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=232)** - Seriously, this simple process of plan, do, check, act does more than just give value in generating improvements.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=240)** It's just as much about teaching people critical [[Thinking Skills]].
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=244)** Toyota refers to this as building people before building cars.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=248)** - The third way of DevOps is largely based on kaizen, so it's a great source of ideas on how to tangibly implement this kind of continuous learning environment.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=258)** In fact, why don't you start now?
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=260)** There's a notebook function in one of the tabs on the course page.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=263)** You can use it to take notes as we go on in the course on small, tangible next steps that you think you can take to make headway in iterating towards DevOps.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/devops-foundations-23454205/continuous-learning-the-devops-way?u=76281980&t=273)** - And that's the third component of a culture that will make it much easier to be successful at DevOps as you start to implement the many technical practices that it provides.
